If you are a software engineer or aspire to become one, you must have heard of Amazon. Amazon is not just an e-commerce giant, but one of the worlds leading tech companies. At the beginning of 2024, Amazons hiring process was somewhat slow. However, by the end of the year, Amazon outpaced all other MAANG companies in terms of hiring, whether on-campus or off-campus. And as we enter the beginning of 2025, there are still openings for the SDE-1 profile on their portal. If you wish to join Amazon, now could be an ideal opportunity. We will also explore the career trajectory once you join the company. Stay tuned, and don't forget to like the video before you begin watching. Lets get started. One of Amazon's most prominent roles is SDE-1, Software Development Engineer 1, and many freshers enter the company in this role. In this position, the CTC (Cost to Company) is 48 LPA, which includes stock options over four years. We will break this down further. The annual compensation is approximately 28 LPA. Lets go through the details: Amazon offers a base salary of 19.2 lakhs. The sign-on bonus for the first year is 6.5 lakhs, and for the second year, its 5 lakhs. The stock value is 15.5 lakhs, which vests over four years: 5% in the first year, 15% in the second year, 40% in the third year, and 40% in the fourth year. Additional benefits, such as relocation allowances, amount to 1.5 lakhs. The total compensation for one year is 28 lakhs. This role is perfect for those who enjoy coding. But what if you dont like coding? Does Amazon have roles for you too? Yes, Amazon also hires freshers for the role of Business Analyst. Many B.Tech and MCA graduates join Amazon in this position. Coding skills are not a requirement here. Instead, strong analytical skills are essential. Ive discussed this role in more detail in another video, where I cover various job profiles. Ill provide the link in the "i" button and description for you to watch after this video, so you can learn how to prepare for this role. As a Business Analyst, youll receive a lower package compared to the SDE-1 role. The CTC in this position is 30 LPA, which includes stock options over four years. Lets break it down: The base salary is 14,39,800. The sign-on bonus for the first and second years is 3,55,000 each. RSUs (Restricted Stock Units) amount to 9,43,000, vested over four years. The relocation bonus is 1.5 lakhs. Therefore, the total compensation for one year is around 18.5 lakhs. Now lets talk about the career progression at Amazon. Promotions are structured at Amazon. Here, your growth is based not only on experience but also on performance. Lets take a look at the corporate ladder. You begin as an SDE-1, working on foundational projects. Typically, within 1.5 to 2 years, if your performance is strong, you get promoted to SDE-2, where you take on more complex problems and end-to-end ownership. The next level is SDE-3, where you design large-scale architectures and lead cross-team collaborations. From SDE-3, you have two tracks: either you continue as an individual contributor focusing on coding, or you become an engineering manager, overseeing and managing other people. In terms of salary hikes without promotions, Amazon offers competitive annual increments, typically ranging from 10% to 15%. When it comes to promotions, for example, when transitioning from SDE-1 to SDE-2 or SDE-2 to SDE-3, your base salary approximately doubles, and you also receive stock refreshes. In the cafeteria, youll find a variety of healthy and tasty snack options. However, unlike Google, not everything is free. The snacks are subsidized at a very low rate. One interesting and unique initiative is Amazons Dogs at Work program, where employees can bring their dogs to work at certain office locations worldwide. Amazon also offers employees discounts on Amazon devices like Alexa, Kindle, and Fire TV. Prime membership benefits are available, and employees receive personalized gifts on special occasions such as work anniversaries, birthdays, or when they achieve something significant. Quarterly team trips and parties are also an enjoyable part of working at Amazon. When it comes to gadgets, Amazon provides the latest work laptops and high-end devices, ensuring that employees have the best tools to perform their work efficiently. Now lets discuss Amazons wellness and fitness programs. Amazons wellness programs are impressive. Employees receive discounts and reimbursements for gym memberships, and wellness challenges and events are regularly organized to encourage an active lifestyle. Yoga and meditation sessions are also available at on-site wellness centers. For mental health support, Amazon offers confidential counseling services and mental health programs. Just like other companies, Amazon offers regular salary hikes, insurance, leaves, shuttle services, and many other perks. Now, lets take a look at how Amazon employees have rated the company on Ambition Box. For Job security it got 3.8 out of 5,for Work life balance it got 3.9 out of 5, for Company's culture 4.2 out of 5, for Skill & Self-Growth 3.8 out of 5 and for Salary & Promotions it got 3.8 out of 5. If youve seen my previous videos about Google and TCS, you might notice that these ratings are somewhat lower. There are several factors that explain this difference. I heard from an Amazon VP that Amazon is a consumer-first company. This means that every decision made at Amazon is primarily focused on the consumers needs. You can think of it this way: in any discussion, the consumer always has a seat at the table. In contrast, companies like Google are employee-first, where employee well-being is given top priority. The reason for this distinction is simple: Amazon operates with very low profit margins and needs to scale quickly. Its a fast-paced company, which contributes to its tough work culture. Additionally, there is the concept of PIP (Performance Improvement Plan). If an employee doesnt perform well for several quarters, they are placed on PIP, and many employees leave the company as a result. This creates pressure to perform consistently well, making the work environment highly competitive. Because of this intense pressure, many employees feel that Amazons work-life balance can be challenging. However, one of the benefits of joining Amazon as a fresher is the recognition you gain from having Amazon on your resume. It opens doors to many opportunities at other companies because it shows that youve worked in a consumer-first environment, can handle pressure, and have the skills to thrive in challenging situations. Another important update is the implementation of the return-to-office policy. During the COVID-19 pandemic, many employees got accustomed to working from home, but now companies are gradually calling employees back to the office. Amazon has also implemented a 5-day work-from-office policy. This change has led to some negative feedback from employees, as many had grown accustomed to working from home. Returning to the office after getting used to remote work has been challenging for some, which explains the lower ratings. Weve already discussed the salary, company perks, growth opportunities, and ratings, but its equally important to understand what Amazon actually does. While most of you know Amazon as an e-commerce platform, the company generates revenue from a variety of sources and workflows. Amazon is a global tech giant that offers Amazon Web Services (AWS), one of the companys most rapidly evolving products. In addition, Amazon provides digital streaming services through Amazon Prime and Amazon Music. The company also creates devices like Alexa, which operate on artificial intelligence. Jeff Bezos started Amazon in 1994 as an online bookstore, and it has since grown into one of the worlds largest tech companies. AWS, in particular, plays a significant role in Amazon's success. In fact, we use AWS to host our platforms and websites. Now, lets take a look at Amazons global presence. Headquartered in Seattle, USA, Amazon employs over 1.6 million people worldwide in 2024. In India, Amazon has major operations with offices in cities like Bangalore, Hyderabad, Chennai, Pune, Mumbai, and Gurgaon. Being a global company, Amazon offers extensive exposure. You get the opportunity to collaborate with teams from various countries, including China and the US. Many employees also transfer to the Seattle office after spending some time working in India. Every year, Amazon hires a significant number of freshers, and compared to companies like Microsoft and Google, Amazon's hiring tends to be higher. In 2023, the company experienced some slowdown due to the economic recession, but things began to pick up in 2024. As of 2025, hiring is still aggressive, and new job openings are available, so make sure to check them out. Now, lets talk about how Amazon hires. First, lets cover on-campus hiring. Initially, Amazon focused on tier-1 colleges like IIT, NSIT, DTU, and certain NITs. Because of their high demands and increased hiring, Amazon has started recruiting from tier-3 colleges as well. The hiring pattern has changed a bit. Initially, they used to hire both interns and full-time employees, but now their primary focus is to hire interns. In the final semester of the final year, Amazon offers 6-month internships, and based on these internships, they provide pre-placement offers and full-time job offers. This gives Amazon sufficient time to assess whether the intern is credible and suitable for a full-time role. After the layoffs caused by the economic slowdown, Amazon, like other tech giants, does not want to repeat the same mistake. They want to ensure they dont hire people who may need to be fired later. Now, let's discuss the hiring process. It usually starts with an online assessment where you need to solve two DSA-based questions. Following that, there is a behavioral test, which focuses on how you handle conflicts, prioritize tasks, and manage stress or work under pressure. Amazon places a lot of value on an individuals personality, which is evaluated based on their leadership principles. These principles are a key focus during Amazons interviews. After clearing the online round, youll have one or two technical interviews, each lasting about 45 minutes. These interviews typically consist of moderate-level DSA questions, mainly sourced from LeetCodes medium or occasionally hard problems. There are two advantages of the campus hiring process. First, you're competing against a smaller pool of candidates, which makes it slightly easier to crack the interviews. Second, if you receive an offer through campus recruitment, the company has a strong relationship with the college, and they are unlikely to revoke your offer. This is because they want to maintain their connection with the college for future hiring and know that they will return next year to recruit top candidates from there. Now, lets move on to the off-campus hiring process. The interview process is almost identical to the campus recruitment process: an online test, followed by technical interviews that assess your DSA knowledge and behavioral questions based on Amazons leadership principles. However, the competition here is more intense because youll be competing with all off-campus candidates. Since Amazon doesnt visit many colleges, all off-campus candidates from across the country will be competing for the same role. Don't underestimate candidates from tier-3 collegesthere are some excellent coders from these colleges, including 6-star, 5-star, expert, and candidate master coders. Therefore, the competition becomes tougher, but the process remains the same. To apply, you can visit Amazon's career portal, where job postings for different roles and locations are frequently updated. You can also apply directly by using the job ID provided in the listings. If you want a referral, you can reach out to Amazon employees on LinkedIn. When asking for a referral, make sure to demonstrate your coding knowledge or share your track record of solving coding problems. Write a concise message explaining your skills and why you're a good fit for the role. Next, lets discuss Amazons summer internship program. This internship lasts for 2 months, and the interview process is nearly identical to the on-campus and off-campus hiring processes. The difficulty level of the questions and interviews is also similar. Based on your performance, youll have the option to choose between a 2-month internship or a full-time offer. However, since Amazon does not offer full-time roles directly from the summer internship, you will have the option to choose a 6-month internship after the 2-month internship, which will lead to a full-time offer. Amazon also offers a program called Amazon WoW (Women of the World), specifically for female students. The details of this program are displayed on the screen, and you can pause the video to read more about it. Additionally, Amazon hires through coding competitions, one of which is Amazon Hackon. This hackathon is designed for pre-final and final-year students, where participants are given real-world problems to solve. Based on their performance, Amazon may offer full-time roles. The process is conducted through Unstop, and Amazon reaches out to the participants to incorporate them into the hiring process. The procedures for the 2-month and 6-month software development internships are similar to those for regular hiring. Another program offered by Amazon is the ML Summer School, which is specifically for data science students. Though not related to software development roles, the ML Summer School offers machine learning enthusiasts hands-on experience with ML concepts and practical applications. Students who join this program typically receive a 2-month internship opportunity as an applied scientist intern. The hiring process for this program follows a similar path to the software development roles. Now, lets talk about Amazons exit process. Leaving Amazon is straightforward but can be both easy and difficult. Its a simple process: you need to discuss your decision with your manager and send an official resignation email. Your manager might try to convince you to stay, but if you have a valid reasonsuch as a better opportunity or the desire to start something of your ownthe process will go smoothly. Youll need to serve a notice period of 30 days to hand over any pending work and documentation. If you are at the L6 level or higher, the notice period is extended to 60 days, as you will have more responsibilities that need to be transferred to other employees. On your last working day, all your company-provided gadgets will be collected, and your team may give you a farewell party. There is also a 6-month cooling-off period before you can rejoin Amazon, which means you cannot join the company again within 6 months. Unlike Google, where you can rejoin without an interview after a year, Amazon requires you to go through the full interview process again if you wish to reapply. Thats all about Amazon. I hope you found this video informative. If you liked it, please comment and let me know which company's analysis you'd like to see next. If youre enjoying this series, Ive already made videos on TCS and Google, and you can find the links in the description. Dont forget to like and share this video with your friends. See you in the next one!

How can software handle billions of payments without missing a single transaction? Today we're going to talk about the Uber engineers solution to. Billions and billions of payments. and easily explain how it all works. So let's go. Now we all know how Uber works. Click a button that pays adjusted money for a leaf from one place to another. Billions of rides and hundreds of billions worth of money being passed around later. And then our easy solution is no longer an easy solution. As Uber grew and grew in popularity, they would evolve their tech stack, going from a monolith application aka just one big application. They deployed to a microservice. One which is like thousands of applications all over the place. They'd switch to Postgres and MySQL. And just build technology everywhere around it. However, if there's one thing that you just can't mess up in your text hack, it's what's dealing with money. their system was messing up big time. first it was just beyond unstable. The system was fragmented and multiple different areas and services transactions were really, really slow. then reconciling transactions was just an absolute nightmare. Payment discrepancies and just major delays were everywhere. Imagine being an Uber driver, driving and giving rise for two days straight. Then a cyberattack happens and then all your payments that you've been expecting for the last few days, it's just gone. Nowhere to be seen, nowhere collected. So they rebuilt their payment system from scratch. First, they switched their system to a job order system. The job in this case represents the trip that you go on. Or an Uber Eats order. This job system allowed flexibility in having multiple orders assigned to the same job. So, for example, asking to stop at McDonald's before getting home. We've all been there. It's it's okay to admit it. Inside these orders are entries, which represents money moving from a payer to app. The sum always zero. No creating or destroying money. So if I paid $20 for an Uber ride, it would come up in two different items. trip fare, which is $18, and the service fee, which is $2. This then goes into the Uber drivers account and then Uber's account. Trip fare 18. Service fee $2. This essentially is how double entry accounting works. Credit and debit. I've covered so many different types of databases on my channel in the past, but none have specifically been designed to tailor towards the need of money or finance. So like, how would you even do that in the first place? A ledger. A line by line table of your transactions. Don't ask the crypto people what a ledger means. What makes ledger still popular to this day is that it's the only way to truly know where you're financially. If my bank account starts at $100 and ends at $1,000, but the purchases and depositors don't end in $1,000, well, some suss stuff is happening in my bank account. doing two seconds of research on this, I can see that, you know, Postgres or MySQL is clearly capable of doing something like this. So why isn't it suitable for finance? Well, first, most databases aren't immutable. if I wanted to change my name on any website, once I change it on the form, the database goes to the existing entry and then updates it, removing the previous value. This is because it is mutable. if I were to try this on an immutable database, it would have to create a brand new row with the new information and duplicate existing information. Then in the UI, I would have to grab the latest version of this. So obviously this is just not good and so wasteful. If you had a database of transactions and then they all equal to zero, and then some dingus deleted a row out of that database. you forever screwed up the integrity of your books. This transaction is just gone forever. So an immutable system would force an append only system, meaning that if a mistake happens, the correction is appended at the bottom of the database. Rather than deleting the record completely. For example, if I were to document a transaction, I could buy lunch for $10. That's -$10 from my account. However, the deli accidentally charged me $15. So am I. Can't you see -$15? Well, rather than just deleting the records and trying again, the deli has to refund me $5, which then turns into a credit on my account. You fix things by adding or subtracting to the end, not by replacing. popular open source options exist like IMDb, but at scale. Uber made the classic programing decision to make their own version from scratch, so they created ledger store. ledger store as an application layer that sits above existing technologies like NoSQL databases. It specifically adds three core concepts. Ceiling closes a time range of changes. This means that transactions that happened last month, you can look at and validate that they are correct, making them now read only. Uber specifically mentioned that they have 30 minute spans of seals. Manifest are files generated and the sealing process. This is a security measure to show that only ledger store can access seal transactions in the past. Just remember though, transactions are happening every second, so they use Apache Kafka, which helps the streaming of this data in real time to calculate and revisions. As for when, sometimes the data needs to be corrected in an already closed time range. Revision is like a table that shows the corrections that have happened while also making the previous additions Queryable. And leisure store. It was great. but Uber had a really, really big problem. You see, Leisure Store was built to be an opinionated about its underlying technology. So when they moved to their new internal database, they had to migrate over 250 billion records. And so they only had two options process all of this 300 terabyte of data in one go and then just dump it into their new database, or break down historical data into parts and process them individually and create checkpoints throughout. The issue with doing number one is that with such a big data, at any point that it goes wrong, you have to restart the entire process. Think about installing a software for a long time and then it just fails. On the last step. So they went with option two and here's how it worked. A worker boots up and reads the checkpoint of where the process needs to be started from. it then goes to cold storage where the data lives and processes this data and moves it to the new database, and then updates the checkpoint to say that the partition it filled out is successful so it doesn't get repeated. And it then stores this in a metadata database so that other simultaneous workers don't work on the same ones. And this process only allowed that data to take a couple of weeks and saved on a lot of money. have our historical data taken care of on a separate database. But how do we put this over live onto one of the busiest applications of all time? This is when Uber introduced the Shadow Rider. The Shadow Rider sits in between two databases, the current one and the one they wanted to migrate over to. The Shadow Rider pushes data to the main database as usual, synchronously, everything executed in order to keep things fast. The Shadow Rider pushes data to the new database asynchronously, meaning our system isn't dependent on if it saves right. The second. but here's another issue. What happens if the items fail? I'm. because it's asynchronous. We don't know if it's going to work or not work. To prevent this, they deployed a spot repair job to look at any issues and fix them on the spot. They also created a dual read and merge system. This reads both databases at the same time and compares the two requests. If the primary database had five records and the secondary had three, it would merge the objects together and say that to the secondary database and return to the user. This put the new database into production gradually to see how it handles under the pressure of a production system, but eventually that leap of faith was needed to be done. So they finally decided to commit to the new databases and made the switch. dock store being the primary and then Dynamo being the secondary. Gradually, less requests were being read from Dynamo and Doc Store continue to grow and grow. Oh, and thank God for that. But why all of this work? Just to change databases. When we talk about the ledger, we can think of it like a piece of paper. With each row dedicated to a new entry. I mean, makes sense for like 50 transactions. But what about trillions of transactions over billions of ledgers? Indexes. Now imagine this scenario. You walk into a movie store and you want a copy of the movie jaws. The cashier says, one moment and one by one, make sure that each movie in a gigantic pile of movies is jaws. I mean, you would be there forever. It's just stupid. An index in a database would be categorizing each movie by the first letter or by genre. So if I ask for jaws, you already know to look at aisle J, But in this case 26 I think 26 indexes are just not going to cut it. And this is why Uber has trillions of indexes that they have managed in their database systems. And there's different types. A strongly consistent indexes used to handle credit card authorization. When you use Uber, your credit card has a hold on it until the end of your trip. If the database isn't able to look up the whole fast, It risks charging you again and continuing this hold. Yikes. This is done with an intricate write and read process. First, ledger store preps the indexes that will be inserting a database record. Once it's prepped, it writes the record and if it's successful, will commit the indexes needed. They found that their indexes get stuck in the intent phase. So to counteract this, if they read that there's a record in the database, they commit the index. Or if it doesn't it rolls back the index. A lot goes into making this extremely reliable. eventual consistent indexes. As for parts of the application that doesn't require extreme precision. So these could be places like previous rides greens where waiting a little bit is fine as long as you get the end result. Think about a ledger for a second. One of the biggest key columns you could probably think of, if not the most important one, is date and time. In this case you can move data from hot storage. Think like OneDrive. Great. But how do we manage 2 trillion of them? After the index is created, it back fills itself with historical data. the change blocks of data event Bridge schedules these snapshots daily or hourly depending on how critical your data is because manual backups are prone to human error and here is exactly how we build it firstly we tag all the important ec2 instances with the flag of backup true this tag based approach gives us flexibility you can easily add or remove instances from the backup schedule without changing any code then we can write a Lambda function that does three things when event Bridge triggers it firstly it finds all the instances with our backup tag this makes the system Dynamic and scalable secondly it creates new snapshots and labels them with metadata such as data time and environment which is crucial for tracking and order to and thirdly it deletes any snapshots older than backups in different regions which is critical for Disaster Recovery scenarios as I always say data is the new oil and with this Cloud project you're showing you know how to save companies thousands
